Before I use it, I spray the head with a Oster Kool Lube. This is similar to the Remington Shaver Saver, but the Oster Kool Lube is much, much cheaper. I bought the Oster Kool Lube (14 oz) at my local Sally Beauty Supply store for $10.99.<br /><br />I don't know if the more expensive Panasonic models are worth it since the Panasonic ES-RT51-s does everything that I would expect from an expensive one.<br /><br />I give this my highest recommendation!<br /><br />UPDATE: After two years, the razor died after water somehow entered the case and damaged the battery. Now I will be able to charge my shaver and/or a set AA batteries. This all would be avoidable if Panasonic would make the entire line of shavers using the standard AA battery. Make money selling shavers and have HAPPY HAPPY customers, instead of ending the experience with a $20+ set of batteries. For $40 I have a whole new shaver as a back up, and plenty of time for modifications to my new charging system. Thus, the path chosen.

So I only had to charge it once every 5 days. Charging was much faster than my old razor at about 20 minutes. The charge level drops in 20% increments. But within about 6 months I noticed that the razor did not perform well when the power reached about 20%. Within a year that symptom started at 40%. Now, at about 16 months the razor dies once it reaches 80%. The battery is clearly dying. The case is sealed, so there is no way to replace it. And unlike my old razors, it cannot be used while plugged in to a wall outlet. This is the case with most electric razors these days. The only option is to purchase a new razor. I really can't justify paying $50 or more each year for a new electric razor. So I've decided to go back to using an old fashioned safety razor. The shave is much closer than electric or cartridge razors, the blades are readily available and relatively inexpensive. It takes a little longer to shave with a safety razor and there is more razor burn. But in the long run, it's a lot cheaper and better for the environment.

  367. I received this shaver as a surprise Christmas gift (meaning I hadn't picked it out or even expected to get one). Another review notes that the battery life is extremely poor. Based on my experience with it, however, I must conclude that he had a faulty unit. In fact, the battery life is one of the most impressive things about this device. Its capacity is indicated in 20% increments on a little LCD panel on the front, and it took a couple shaves to even reach 80%. It also retains its charge pretty well. Personally, I'd prefer 10% increments, but at least a &#34;plug&#34; icon starts blinking when the device needs a recharge. It also won't operate when plugged in, but this is standard for wet-dry shavers, as a safety measure. The lower part of the shaver becomes slightly warm during recharging.<br /><br />You'll also notice in the promotional image that there's two black buttons on the side of the head. There are corresponding buttons on the other side of the shaver's head. The top set releases the foil (to replace it if damaged, or to wash it separately), while the lower set partially removes the housing around the head, so you can more easily clean the blade assembly. I definitely recommend keeping a stiff-bristle brush on hand, because running water won't clean it up completely. The head itself is not removable. During use, it can tilt left and right and can be pushed in slightly, so it has some &#34;give&#34; when applying pressure to stubborn hair.<br /><br />It's a shame that Panasonic forces you to buy proprietary battery replacements from them at $20 a pop. It's another $20 or so to replace the blades. And there's the foil as well. Strikes me as a bit expensive in the long run, considering how basic this shaver is.<br /><br />Side note: If you pass the shaver over some hair several times and it doesn't get cut, the hair is probably too long to get properly caught by the blades. Use the beard trimmer on it, then shave that spot like usual. The hair should disappear.<br /><br />Update 8/9/2015: Sadly, this shaver conked out a few months ago, despite infrequent usage. Even with it plugged in for several hours, I could only get a faint hum and no blade movement. So I have to downgrade this review from the four-star rating of &#34;I like it&#34; to the two-star rating of &#34;I don't like it.&#34; Maybe it just needs a new battery, but I'm not interested in paying another chunk of money to find out. It shouldn't need another this soon., this shaver conked out a few months ago, despite infrequent usage. Even with it plugged in for several hours, I could only get a faint hum and no blade movement. So I ended up ditching this one and bought the ES8103S, which is the cheapest Linear Drive model with a battery meter that I am aware of. And the difference has been like night and day.<br /><br />I realize that different shavers can have different effect depending on who's using them, as everyone has different faces and facial hairs. But if you want to make a safer bet for your money, I'd say go with a Linear Drive.

  406. I've used just about every Panasonic wet/dry shaver they make. Without exception, they have all failed after approximately two years (just past the warranty period, ironically.)<br /><br />I recently purchased this model to replace a dead 82xx model, and found that it is equal in shave quality to the very expensive Panasonic models with all the self-cleaning jazz. In fact, I don't intend to do anything more than basic rinses any more, and occasionally clean underneath the cutters.<br /><br />You see, I bought the high-dollar version last time, thinking that I'd be compulsive about cleaning it, thereby causing it to last forever. I meticulously cleaned it, replaced the foil and cutter, etc., and it still died in predictable fashion after 25 months. I actually laughed when it stopped cutting in mid-shave!<br /><br />The failure mode on all 5 of my Panasonics (yes, 10.5 years worth!) has been the center cutting bar mechanism. The plastic piece which extends out from the head and moves the blade back and forth eventually wears out inside the head. Although it will still vibrate, it does not put enough force on the cutting bar and it will just remain motionless. Replacing the blade(s) has no effect on the longevity of this part. Adding oil to the blades doesn't seem to make it last longer either. It is quite obviously designed to fail.<br /><br />I tried an experiment with keeping the same blade for about a year, then comparing it with a new blade (foil, cutter, etc.) I honestly couldn't tell the difference in closeness, however, the new foil seemed to move more smoothly over my face and maybe it had an easier time when I'd let my beard grow out a few days.<br /><br />Fortunately, I have a backup rotary shaver that I keep charged. It cuts slower and not quite as closely, but keeps me from getting to work half-shaved when I forget to recharge.<br /><br />So, I will summarize thus:<br /><br />This shaver provides an excellent, close shave. It requires many, many passes over the same area in different directions due to its design, but it eventually does the job. If you shave every day, it works much better. I have used it with just water, no water, and with the Total Shaving solution oil drops, and by far the oil drops are the best possible choice (for me.) That's different for everyone, but if you haven't tried it, I recommend a sample.<br /><br />Compared to my rotary shaver, the Panasonic is slightly louder in volume. The buzzing is considerably quieter with this model than with my 82xx, and that surprised me when I first turned it on. The rotary takes fewer passes over the same area of my face, however it doesn't quite get as close as the Panasonic, so I'd rather take the extra two minutes and get a closer cut.<br /><br />The pop-up trimmer is handy and effective. My main complaint with it is that it is awkwardly located, making really accurate cuts somewhat difficult. If you use it often you'll get used to it. I use it for emergency sideburn trims, but I'd probably stay away from any precise mustache work at first.<br /><br />The other comparison is with disposable razor shaving. I rarely shave with them, but they are exceptionally close, and once the blood stops flowing, I notice the shaver cut isn't quite a match for a good old Mach 3. The Mach 3/4/5, whatever they are now, is tremendously faster, very messy, and tough for me to use in a shower with no mirror. For me, since my skin never gets used to it (tried for many years), I prefer the electric overall.<br /><br />So, bottom line. Get the cheap Panasonic, and if you want wet/dry then this is the one. If you just need dry, then you can go even cheaper and still get the exact same shave quality. Don't let the gimmicks fool you, it's the same plastic, same motor, same mechanism, same shave. You can make a difference by choosing some skin preparation oil and keeping the blade basically clean.

Comfortable, close shaves and quieter than most.<br /><br />BTW, the key to longer cutter and head life for any &#34;wet and dry&#34; shaver is to never use it wet because even fine stainless steel corrodes more readily in the presence of water. Just clean frequently with a soft brush and compressed air. And, with replacement shaver heads so expensive (all brands), your best approach on one in this moderate price range is to use it as long you get satisfactory shaves then buy a new one. That gets you a new device, under warranty, for very little more than the replacement parts. Panasonic shavers are a great value.

The problem is the battery - it is deteriorating rapidly. The shaver has an LCD display that shows the approximate charge remaining in 20% increments. For the first few months I could run the battery down to 0% before the shaver would stop. Then after a few more months it would shut off at 20%. Now several more months later, it runs down to 40% and shuts off. The shaver uses a Lithium ion battery, not the outmoded Nickel Cadmium type that most cheap-quality, battery-powered consumer products come with. At this rate of deterioration, I'll be back to using the old Braun I replaced with this piece of Chicom Crap when the old Panasonic ES3041 died!
